###xml 680 692 680 692 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. simulans,</italic>
###xml 783 791 783 791 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HDC14862</italic>
###xml 795 810 795 810 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 873 879 873 879 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG2708</italic>
###xml 905 907 905 907 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d,</italic>
###xml 957 958 957 958 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 962 974 962 974 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. simulans,</italic>
###xml 1018 1026 1018 1026 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HDC14862</italic>
###xml 1107 1115 1107 1115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050152-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1152 1170 1152 1170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In(3R)84F1;93F6&#8211;7,</italic>
###xml 1211 1228 1211 1228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HDC14862, pfd800,</italic>
###xml 1233 1242 1233 1242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HDC12400,</italic>
###xml 1349 1358 1349 1358 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HDC14862.</italic>
###xml 171 182 <span type="species:ncbi:7240">D. simulans</span>
###xml 411 422 <span type="species:ncbi:7240">D. simulans</span>
###xml 504 519 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 680 691 <span type="species:ncbi:7240">D. simulans</span>
###xml 795 810 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 962 973 <span type="species:ncbi:7240">D. simulans</span>
In the case of In(3R)84F1;93F6-7, four breaks (a, b, c, and d in Figure 1) would have occurred in an ancestral chromosomal arrangement that is now best represented in the D. simulans genome. The breakpoint pairs a-c and b-d (which have been confirmed by resequencing; Figure 1) would each represent staggered breaks within a single chromatid in Figure 2. CG2708 and HDC14862 overlap by 56-59 base pairs (bp) in D. simulans. Breakpoint a occurred at the 5' end of this overlap, duplicating this region in D. melanogaster. Breakpoint b occurred in the region between HDC12400 and HDC14861. Breakpoint c occurred downstream of the "exon" 2 of the distal, partial copy of HDC14862 in D. simulans, which roughly corresponds to the intron between "exons" 2 and 3 of the "complete" copy of HDC14862 of D. melanogaster (roughly upstream of the start of the overlapping region with CG2708). The fourth breakpoint, d, is found 1,760-1,764 bp downstream of breakpoint c in D. simulans, at 25 bp from the start of the "exon" 1 of HDC14862. End-filling followed by nonhomologous end joining in the inverted orientation (Figure 2) would result in both the inversion In(3R)84F1;93F6-7, the duplication of the region including HDC14862, pfd800, and HDC12400, and the fortuitous formation of what is considered a "complete" copy of the putatively expressed sequence HDC14862.
###end p 23
###begin title 24
###xml 52 67 52 67 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 72 81 72 81 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 52 67 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 72 81 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Comparative Analysis of Genome Organization between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 110 125 110 125 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 130 140 130 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba.</italic>
###xml 146 161 146 161 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 221 224 221 224 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;30</sup>
###xml 272 281 272 281 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 368 383 368 383 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 410 419 410 419 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 633 641 633 641 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t001">Tables 1</xref>
###xml 853 855 853 855 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b065">65</xref>
###xml 982 990 982 990 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st002">Table S2</xref>
###xml 1074 1089 1074 1089 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1094 1103 1094 1103 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1117 1125 1117 1125 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050152-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 1177 1186 1177 1186 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-sg004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 1361 1363 1361 1363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b066">66</xref>
###xml 110 125 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 130 139 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 146 161 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 272 281 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 368 383 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 410 419 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1074 1089 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1094 1103 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
We used a computational approach to identify genome-wide disruptions in gene order between the chromosomes of D. melanogaster and D. yakuba. Each D. melanogaster transcript was used as a query in a high stringency (E < 10-30) BLASTN search against the genomic sequence of D. yakuba. This allowed us to map unambiguously 12,690 genes (94.4% of those of Release 4.1) of D. melanogaster on the genome sequence of D. yakuba. A comparison of the gene orders of the two species identified 55 gene-order disruptions between them, which appear as discontinuities in the coordinates of neighboring genes in one species relative to the other (Tables 1 and S1). All predicted gene-order disruptions identified using this gene-based BLAST approach are also identified as termini of whole-genome global alignments at the University of California, Santa Cruz (UCSC) [65]. These 55 gene-order disruptions define 59 syntenic blocks between these species (since both species have four chromosomes) (Table S2). The location and relative orientation of the syntenic blocks for chromosome 2 of D. melanogaster and D. yakuba are shown in Figure 3; similar data are shown for chromosomes X and 3 in Figure S4. We do not show the small chromosome 4 (syntenic block 59), since our results indicate that this chromosome is wholly collinear in the two species over the sequenced region [66]. Syntenic blocks 13, 26, and 46 include the centromeric heterochromatic regions for chromosomes X, 2, and 3, respectively. We are unable, given the present sequence data, to detect any chromosome rearrangements within these heterochromatic regions or those on chromosome 4.
###end p 25
###begin p 26
###xml 163 172 163 172 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 213 229 213 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster,</italic>
###xml 318 328 318 328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 398 419 398 419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 478 486 478 486 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st001">Table S1</xref>
###xml 641 650 641 650 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 692 701 692 701 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 872 881 872 881 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 886 901 886 901 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 163 172 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 213 228 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 318 327 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 641 650 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 692 701 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 872 881 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 886 901 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
To obviate possible artifacts of the assembly process (see Material and Methods) on our results, and directly confirm our predictions of the gene order around the D. yakuba breakpoint regions relative to those of D. melanogaster, we cloned and sequence verified a sample of 27 of the predicted breakpoint regions from D. yakuba, each containing the transition between adjacent syntenic blocks (see Materials and Methods). In every case, our predictions were directly confirmed (Table S1). This result is consistent with the fact that all predicted gene-order disruptions are found in high-quality, contiguous (i.e., ungapped) regions of the D. yakuba assembly. In fact, breakpoint regions in D. yakuba are sequenced to an average depth of 8x and are supported by an average of 14 clone pairs. These results demonstrate that the gene-order disruptions inferred between the D. yakuba and D. melanogaster genomes are not assembly artifacts.
###end p 26
###begin p 27
###xml 42 57 42 57 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 91 100 91 100 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 297 312 297 312 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 338 347 338 347 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 567 583 567 583 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster,</italic>
###xml 599 608 599 608 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 855 870 855 870 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 915 924 915 924 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1046 1047 1044 1045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1060 1063 1058 1061 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;61</sup>
###xml 1250 1265 1248 1263 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1270 1279 1268 1277 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1308 1309 1306 1307 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Z</italic>
###xml 1320 1321 1318 1319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1667 1669 1665 1667 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b026">26</xref>
###xml 1670 1672 1668 1670 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b067">67</xref>
###xml 1816 1817 1814 1815 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</italic>
###xml 1825 1826 1823 1824 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 42 57 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 91 100 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 297 312 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 338 347 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 567 582 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 599 608 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 855 870 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 915 924 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1250 1265 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1270 1279 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Approximately 117.8 megabases (Mb) of the D. melanogaster genome and about 118.9 Mb of the D. yakuba genome are included in the 59 syntenic blocks as defined by their outermost markers or reference genes. The amount of nonheterochromatic DNA not included in these syntenic blocks is 542 kb of the D. melanogaster genome and 674 kb of the D. yakuba genome. This is an upper estimate because in some cases, there is noncoding homology between the reference genes that define two consecutive syntenic blocks (see below). The median size of syntenic blocks is 1.66 Mb in D. melanogaster, and 1.61 Mb in D. yakuba. Excluding the syntenic blocks that contain centromeric heterochromatin (blocks 13, 26, and 46), the largest (syntenic block 57) is just over 6 Mb (~5.2% of the genome in both species), and the smallest is 161 kb (syntenic block 22, 0.08% of the D. melanogaster genome; and syntenic block 25, 0.08% of the D. yakuba genome). The length of genomic regions in each syntenic block is highly correlated across species (Spearman rho = 0.997, p = 3.78 x 10 -61; blocks 13, 26, and 46 not included), and in only two cases (blocks 26 and 43), do they differ by more than 10%. The DNA content per syntenic block does not differ significantly between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba (Wilcoxon signed rank test, Z = -1.273, p = not significant [n.s.]; blocks 13, 26, and 46 not included). A departure of the observed distribution of the lengths of syntenic blocks from that expected if the breakpoints were randomly distributed across the genome (a truncated negative exponential distribution) would allow us to discard the random breakage model of chromosome evolution [26,67]. Based on the comparison of the empirical and theoretical distributions, we cannot reject the random breakage model (Kolmogorov-Smirnov test, D = 0.2, p = n.s.; blocks 13, 26, and 46 not included).
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 190 200 190 200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 229 231 229 231 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b068">68</xref>
###xml 259 261 259 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b069">69</xref>
###xml 262 264 262 264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b071">71</xref>
###xml 321 336 321 336 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 341 351 341 351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 384 391 384 391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">between</italic>
###xml 425 431 425 431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">within</italic>
###xml 449 458 449 458 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st003">Tables S3</xref>
###xml 463 465 463 465 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st004">S4</xref>
###xml 321 336 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 341 350 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Despite the conservative criteria used in our BLAST analysis, its resolution is sufficient to detect gene sequences that may have "escaped" synteny by transposition, as has been observed in Drosophila both experimentally, e.g., [68], and by genomic analyses [69-71]. We detected 22 potential transposition events between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba, with 12 occurring unambiguously between chromosome arms and eight events within chromosome arms (Tables S3 and S4). This number is likely to be an underestimate because we used stringent criteria for paralogy. Of the 22 events that we detected, 20 are duplicative transpositions and two are conservative transpositions.
###end p 28
###begin title 29
###xml 48 63 48 63 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 68 77 68 77 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 48 63 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 68 77 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Reconstruction of the Inversion History between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba
###end title 29
###begin p 30
###xml 8 10 8 10 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b034">34</xref>
###xml 79 89 79 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 175 190 175 190 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 473 488 473 488 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 493 502 493 502 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 608 610 608 610 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b054">54</xref>
###xml 613 620 613 620 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 175 190 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 473 488 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 493 502 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Muller [34] defined the six fundamental elements of the karyotype of the genus Drosophila (now referred to as Muller's elements A-F, each corresponding to a chromosome arm of D. melanogaster). The overall gene content of these elements has been conserved during the evolution of the genus as witnessed by the very few inter-element rearrangements (i.e., pericentric inversions and translocations) that have been reported. Previous analysis of inversion differences between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba based on polytene chromosome revealed 28 inversions, of which only one, on chromosome 2 was pericentric [54] (Table 2).
###end p 30
###begin p 31
###xml 196 211 196 211 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 216 225 216 225 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 227 236 227 236 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050152-g003">Figures 3</xref>
###xml 245 253 245 253 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st001">Table S1</xref>
###xml 415 417 415 417 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b054">54</xref>
###xml 482 497 482 497 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 502 512 502 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 607 614 607 614 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 743 745 743 745 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b054">54</xref>
###xml 884 892 884 892 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t001">Tables 1</xref>
###xml 897 898 897 898 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t002">2</xref>
###xml 196 211 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 216 225 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 482 497 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 502 511 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
We established which pairs of breakpoint regions define particular inversions by taking into account the contiguity relationships in both species of the outermost genes of syntenic blocks between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba (Figures 3 and S4; Table S1). In general, our computational analysis of the genome sequences of these two species is broadly compatible with previous results based on polytene chromosomes [54]. We inferred that 29 inversions distinguish the chromosomes of D. melanogaster and D. yakuba, of which 28 are paracentric and one corresponds to the pericentric inversion on chromosome 2 (Table 2). The total number of inversions inferred computationally is just one more than that suggested by polytene chromosome analysis [54], although the greater resolution of the sequence analysis increases the number of breakpoints from 48 to 55 and refines their positions (Tables 1 and 2).
###end p 31
###begin p 32
###xml 81 83 81 83 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b054">54</xref>
###xml 86 94 86 94 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t001">Tables 1</xref>
###xml 99 100 99 100 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t002">2</xref>
###xml 202 214 202 214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">melanogaster</italic>
###xml 286 288 286 288 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b054">54</xref>
###xml 357 366 357 366 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 386 410 386 410 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. teissieri, D. erecta,</italic>
###xml 415 424 415 424 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. orena,</italic>
###xml 430 445 430 445 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 475 486 475 486 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. simulans</named-content>
###xml 506 514 506 514 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050152-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 641 643 641 643 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b054">54</xref>
###xml 769 778 769 778 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 783 792 783 792 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. erecta</named-content>
###xml 859 867 859 867 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st005">Table S5</xref>
###xml 937 944 937 944 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 1018 1027 1018 1027 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1032 1041 1032 1041 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. erecta</named-content>
###xml 1092 1113 1092 1113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">melanogaster-simulans</italic>
###xml 1123 1132 1123 1132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-sg006">Figure S6</xref>
###xml 357 366 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 386 398 <span type="species:ncbi:7243">D. teissieri</span>
###xml 400 409 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
###xml 415 423 <span type="species:ncbi:7233">D. orena</span>
###xml 430 445 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 475 486 <span type="species:ncbi:7240">D. simulans</span>
###xml 769 778 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 783 792 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
###xml 1018 1027 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1032 1041 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
Our analysis shows many discrepancies in detail when compared to previous work ([54]; Tables 1 and 2). This is especially true on the X chromosome, where the banding pattern has diverged greatly in the melanogaster species group. On chromosome 2, there is what Lemeunier and Ashburner [54] interpreted as a single pericentric inversion, which distinguishes D. yakuba and its relatives, D. teissieri, D. erecta, and D. orena, from D. melanogaster and the three species of the D. simulans clade. As shown in Figure 3, there is a complex mosaic of syntenic blocks between the two arms of chromosome 2. In good agreement with the previous work [54], a single pericentric inversion, 2LR(5), is sufficient to explain this pattern. This inversion has identical limits in both D. yakuba and D. erecta. Inverted duplications at the breakpoint regions in both species (Table S5, see below) and information on gene order in other outgroup species (Table 1) strongly suggest that this inversion occurred in the common ancestor of D. yakuba and D. erecta after this lineage split from that leading to the melanogaster-simulans complex. Figure S6 illustrates one of the most parsimonious scenarios that explains the evolution of chromosome 2.
###end p 32
###begin title 33
Inversion-Mediated Duplication Is Frequent at Breakpoint Regions
###end title 33
###begin p 34
###xml 73 82 73 82 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 179 194 179 194 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 199 208 199 208 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 225 234 225 234 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 244 251 244 251 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 427 443 427 443 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster.</italic>
###xml 576 584 576 584 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st005">Table S5</xref>
###xml 643 652 643 652 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 716 726 716 726 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 779 794 779 794 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 853 862 853 862 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 968 985 968 985 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In(3R)84F1;93F6&#8211;7</italic>
###xml 991 999 991 999 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050152-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 73 82 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 179 194 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 199 208 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 225 234 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 427 442 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 643 652 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 779 794 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 853 862 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
We characterized in detail the sequences of the 55 breakpoint regions of D. yakuba because genomic and phylogenetic evidence suggested that virtually all inversion events between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba occurred on the D. yakuba lineage (Table 1; see below). Remarkably, in 34 of 55 (approximately 62%) breakpoint regions, we detected the presence of duplications of sequences that are only present once in the genome of D. melanogaster. In each case, these duplications are specifically associated with the pair of breakpoint regions that limit a particular inversion (Table S5; see below). These duplications are not repetitive in the D. yakuba genome (by BLAST analysis), nor do they match any identifiable Drosophila TE. In a control experiment, the genomic regions of D. melanogaster that correspond to the co-occurrent breakpoint regions of D. yakuba were compared to each other. Repetitive sequences were found in six cases; in no case other than that of In(3R)84F1;93F6-7 (see Figure 1) were duplications of unique sequences found.
###end p 34
###begin p 35
###xml 64 79 64 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster</italic>
###xml 84 93 84 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba</italic>
###xml 376 378 376 378 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b072">72</xref>
###xml 504 511 504 511 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG14817</italic>
###xml 532 538 532 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG6081</italic>
###xml 565 572 565 572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG34034</italic>
###xml 1238 1247 1234 1243 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-sg005">Figure S5</xref>
###xml 1253 1255 1249 1251 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-sg005">S5</xref>
###xml 1326 1335 1322 1331 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1438 1446 1434 1442 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st005">Table S5</xref>
###xml 64 79 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 84 93 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1326 1335 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
In total, 18 of 29 inversions (approximately 62%) fixed between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba are associated with duplications of sequences included at co-occurrent breakpoint regions. These duplicated sequences are in opposite orientations in the co-occurrent breakpoints of 17 inversions; 3R(6) is the only exception, potentially as a result of a subsequent microinversion [72]. These sequence duplications include 22 full or partial duplications of protein coding genes. Most of these (exceptions are CG14817 at Xy(1) and Xy(4), CG6081 at 2y(15) and 2y(18), and CG34034 at 3y(46) and 3y(53)) have accumulated many point and indel mutations, and are presumed to be nonfunctional. The average nucleotide identity (+/- the standard deviation [SD]) between duplicates is approximately 88% +/- 5.4%. For six of the inversions, sequences from both breakpoint regions are present as inverted duplications at each breakpoint. For the remaining 12 inversions, sequences from only one of the two breakpoint regions are duplicated. This may be due either to the evolutionary loss, by sequence change, of one of the copies of an original duplication, or to the fact that only one of the pair of single-stranded breaks was significantly staggered (Figure S5A and S5B, respectively). The size of the duplications varies significantly in D. yakuba (median = 321 bp, coefficient of variation [CV] = 81% counting only one of the copies when in tandem; Table S5), but in no case do they involve more than about 1.9 kb of aligned sequence (the shortest duplication is 46-bp long).
###end p 35
###begin p 36
###xml 268 270 268 270 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b073">73</xref>
###xml 271 273 271 273 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b074">74</xref>
###xml 319 321 319 321 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b024">24</xref>
###xml 351 353 351 353 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b075">75</xref>
###xml 354 356 354 356 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b078">78</xref>
###xml 386 388 386 388 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b046">46</xref>
###xml 389 391 389 391 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b079">79</xref>
###xml 392 394 392 394 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b081">81</xref>
###xml 400 416 400 416 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster,</italic>
###xml 530 532 530 532 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b082">82</xref>
###xml 659 661 659 661 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b025">25</xref>
###xml 662 664 662 664 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b069">69</xref>
###xml 753 755 753 755 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b025">25</xref>
###xml 756 758 756 758 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b046">46</xref>
###xml 759 761 759 761 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b047">47</xref>
###xml 762 764 762 764 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b051">51</xref>
###xml 874 881 874 881 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t003">Table 3</xref>
###xml 260 266 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeasts</span>
###xml 306 311 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 312 317 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 327 332 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 400 415 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
In many taxa, repeated sequences have been found to be associated with rearrangement breakpoints and have been implicated in mediating chromosomal rearrangements by a process of ectopic exchange. This has been the case for tRNAs and ribosomal protein genes in yeasts [73,74], segmental duplications in the human-mouse [24] and human-primate lineages [75-78], and TEs in many organisms [46,79-81]. In D. melanogaster, there is abundant experimental evidence that exchange between TEs can result in chromosome rearrangement (e.g., [82]). Comparative sequence data also indicate that TEs are abundant at interspecific breakpoint regions between Diptera species [25,69], and there is strong evidence implicating TE-mediated ectopic exchange events in four [25,46,47,51] of the ten well-defined inversions whose breakpoint regions have been characterized at the molecular level (Table 3).
###end p 36
###begin p 37
###xml 38 47 38 47 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 126 141 126 141 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 150 152 150 152 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b083">83</xref>
###xml 232 247 232 247 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 320 329 320 329 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 331 339 331 339 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st006">Table S6</xref>
###xml 505 513 505 513 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st006">Table S6</xref>
###xml 645 654 645 654 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 684 693 684 693 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 743 752 743 752 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 914 923 914 923 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1418 1425 1418 1425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">absence</italic>
###xml 1699 1714 1699 1714 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1719 1728 1719 1728 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba</italic>
###xml 2063 2070 2063 2070 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t003">Table 3</xref>
###xml 38 47 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 126 141 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 232 247 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 320 329 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 645 654 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 684 693 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 743 752 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 914 923 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1699 1714 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1719 1728 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
We analyzed the breakpoint regions of D. yakuba for TE sequences using RepeatMasker with the Release 4.2 TE annotation of the D. melanogaster genome [83] and by BLAST2 analysis using as a query TEs sequences from species other than D. melanogaster. Over 45% of breakpoint regions (25/55) include repetitive sequences in D. yakuba (Table S6), but only five co-occurrent pairs of breakpoint regions (involving inversions 2LR(5), 2L(6), 2LR(8), 3L(3)/3L(4), and 3R(6)) include a similar repetitive sequence (Table S6). These analyses would fail to detect any repetitive sequence absent from the RepeatMasker library (as would be those exclusive to D. yakuba) or not yet characterized in D. yakuba. For this reason, we manually extracted from the D. yakuba breakpoint regions a set of sequences, each corresponding to the precise transition region between syntenic blocks, and used them as BLAST queries to the entire D. yakuba genome. Similar repetitive sequences were found at the co-occurrent breakpoints of the inversions X(1), 2L(6), 3L(5), and 3R(7), although only in the case of 2L(6) and 3R(7) are the copies of the repetitive sequence inverted with respect to each other. The average length of these sequences was 685 bp and the range 49-3,037 bp. Unfortunately, we can neither date the insertion of these repetitive sequences (with respect to the time of occurrence of the inversion), nor can we assert that the absence of repetitive sequences at other pairs of co-occurrent breakpoint regions is not due to their decay or loss subsequent to the occurrence of an inversion. Nevertheless, these data provide little direct evidence for the presence of TEs in generating fixed inversions between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba and, combined with the recurrent presence of inverted duplications of nonrepetitive sequences, suggests that ectopic recombination between TEs has not been the dominant mechanism of generating inversions in this lineage. These results contrast with the presence of inverted TEs at co-occurrent breakpoints of well-defined inversions (Table 3).
###end p 37
###begin title 38
Lineage-Specific Rates of Chromosomal Evolution
###end title 38
###begin p 39
###xml 80 95 80 95 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 99 108 99 108 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 155 162 155 162 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 247 262 247 262 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 270 279 270 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba</italic>
###xml 304 314 304 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 780 790 780 790 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 826 843 826 843 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In(3R)84F1;93F6&#8211;7</italic>
###xml 871 886 871 886 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 939 948 939 948 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. erecta</named-content>
###xml 949 958 949 958 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1026 1027 1026 1027 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1039 1041 1039 1041 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;8</sup>
###xml 1090 1092 1090 1092 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b064">64</xref>
###xml 1371 1387 1371 1387 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. pseudoobscura</named-content>
###xml 1392 1405 1392 1405 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. subobscura</named-content>
###xml 1407 1409 1407 1409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b084">84</xref>
###xml 1420 1435 1420 1435 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1490 1499 1490 1499 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1501 1503 1501 1503 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b054">54</xref>
###xml 1630 1645 1630 1645 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1650 1659 1650 1659 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1661 1663 1661 1663 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b085">85</xref>
###xml 1664 1666 1664 1666 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b086">86</xref>
###xml 80 95 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 99 108 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 247 262 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 270 279 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 780 789 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 871 886 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 939 948 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
###xml 949 958 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1371 1387 <span type="species:ncbi:7237">D. pseudoobscura</span>
###xml 1392 1405 <span type="species:ncbi:7241">D. subobscura</span>
###xml 1420 1435 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1490 1499 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1630 1645 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1650 1659 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
We mapped the derived state of the 29 inversions between the two genomes to the D. melanogaster or D. yakuba lineages, using several independent criteria (Table 1): (1) by determining the arrangement of each gene pair disrupted by an inversion in D. melanogaster versus D. yakuba in five other sequenced Drosophila species; (2) by the presence of inverted duplications associated with co-occurrent breakpoints, as discussed above; and (3) by the disruption of a tandem array of related genes, or of a pair of genes whose transcripts show 3'-overlap (see below), which we also consider to be a derived state. In all cases in which we can use more than one of these criteria, all are consistent. Our analyses show that of 29 inversions, 28 have been fixed in the lineage leading to D. yakuba, and only one (3R(8), also known as In(3R)84F1;93F6-7) on the lineage leading to D. melanogaster (eight of the former inversions occurred before the D. erecta/D. yakuba split). This difference is highly significant (one-tailed binomial p = 5.59 x 10-8) and agrees well with previous interpretations [64], demonstrating that rates of chromosomal evolution can vary by over an order of magnitude even among closely related species. The origin of this very asymmetric rate of fixation cannot stem from differences in the degree of intraspecific polymorphism, as has been proposed for D. pseudoobscura and D. subobscura [84], because D. melanogaster is substantially more polymorphic for inversions than D. yakuba [54]. Rather, it might reflect different effective population sizes between the African populations of the immediate ancestors of D. melanogaster and D. yakuba [85,86].
###end p 39

###xml 1112 1127 1112 1127 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>

###xml 1147 1149 1147 1149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b087">87</xref>
###xml 1158 1181 1158 1181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. virilis, D. montana,</italic>
###xml 1186 1201 1186 1201 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. novamexicana</named-content>
###xml 1203 1205 1203 1205 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b088">88</xref>
###xml 1281 1306 1281 1306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster/D. yakuba</italic>
###xml 1323 1350 1323 1350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster/D. repleta,</italic>
###xml 1396 1398 1396 1398 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b087">87</xref>
###xml 1541 1552 1541 1552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila,</italic>
###xml 1646 1653 1646 1653 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">repleta</italic>
###xml 1669 1671 1669 1671 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b040">40</xref>
###xml 433 448 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 449 458 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 522 538 <span type="species:ncbi:7237">D. pseudoobscura</span>
###xml 539 549 <span type="species:ncbi:7229|species:ncbi:560515">D. miranda</span>
###xml 595 611 <span type="species:ncbi:7237">D. pseudoobscura</span>
###xml 612 625 <span type="species:ncbi:7241">D. subobscura</span>
###xml 728 738 <span type="species:ncbi:7244">D. virilis</span>
###xml 739 749 <span type="species:ncbi:376077|species:ncbi:80423|species:ncbi:127420|species:ncbi:232746|species:ncbi:413762|species:ncbi:173411|species:ncbi:40370|species:ncbi:560718|species:ncbi:199611|species:ncbi:101775">D. montana</span>
###xml 1112 1127 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1132 1142 <span type="species:ncbi:30043">D. repleta</span>
###xml 1158 1168 <span type="species:ncbi:7244">D. virilis</span>
###xml 1170 1180 <span type="species:ncbi:376077|species:ncbi:80423|species:ncbi:127420|species:ncbi:232746|species:ncbi:413762|species:ncbi:173411|species:ncbi:40370|species:ncbi:560718|species:ncbi:199611|species:ncbi:101775">D. montana</span>
###xml 1186 1201 <span type="species:ncbi:47314">D. novamexicana</span>
###xml 1281 1296 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1297 1306 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1323 1338 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1339 1349 <span type="species:ncbi:30043">D. repleta</span>
We used the number of breakpoints per Mb per Myr to correct for differences in chromosomal size in a comparison of rates of chromosomal evolution between species pairs of different Drosophila groups (Table 4) in which we assumed a constant rate of evolution as a null hypothesis. In view of the pericentric changes in chromosome 2 (Muller's elements B+C), we combined the data for these elements. The overall rate of breakage in the D. melanogaster/D. yakuba lineage is 0.0183/Mb/Myr. This is slower than that seen in the D. pseudoobscura/D. miranda (Gadj = 38.9; d.f. = 1; p < 4.4 x 10-10) and D. pseudoobscura/D. subobscura (Gadj = 48.5; d.f. = 1; p < 3.4 x 10-12) comparisons, comparable with the rate seen in the comparison D. virilis/D. montana (Gadj = 0.5; d.f. = 1; p = n.s.) and accelerated with respect to that in the repleta species group (Gadj = 4.3; d.f. = 1; p < 4.3 x 10-9). Across Muller's elements, the rank order of the rate of chromosome evolution is A > (B+C) > E > D, which agrees well with the genus-wide pattern of rates of evolution A > E > D proposed by [87], based on the comparisons of D. melanogaster and D. repleta [21,87] and of D. virilis, D. montana, and D. novamexicana [88]. Nevertheless, Muller's elements B+C appear to have evolved faster in the D. melanogaster/D. yakuba lineage than in D. melanogaster/D. repleta, in which element B was the slowest evolving [87]. Thus, in addition to rate variation among lineages, rates of chromosomal evolution may vary across Muller's elements in different groups of Drosophila, in good agreement with, for example, the fast evolution of the Muller's element E across the repleta species group [40].
###end p 40
###begin title 41
Breakpoint Clustering
###end title 41
###begin p 42
###xml 55 57 55 57 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b054">54</xref>
###xml 58 60 58 60 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b089">89</xref>

###xml 93 95 93 95 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b025">25</xref>
