###xml 99 101 99 101 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b092">92</xref>
###xml 211 218 211 218 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 359 369 359 369 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sophophora</italic>
###xml 392 420 392 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. ananassae, D. persimilis,</italic>
###xml 425 441 425 441 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. pseudoobscura</named-content>
###xml 462 477 462 477 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 579 604 579 604 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster/D. yakuba</italic>
###xml 665 690 665 690 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster/D. yakuba</italic>
###xml 999 1006 999 1006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG9579,</italic>
###xml 1207 1212 1207 1212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sdic,</italic>
###xml 1220 1235 1220 1235 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1245 1247 1245 1247 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b093">93</xref>
###xml 1416 1425 1416 1425 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1559 1574 1559 1574 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1594 1596 1594 1596 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b094">94</xref>
###xml 392 404 <span type="species:ncbi:7217">D. ananassae</span>
###xml 406 419 <span type="species:ncbi:374970|species:ncbi:7234">D. persimilis</span>
###xml 425 441 <span type="species:ncbi:7237">D. pseudoobscura</span>
###xml 462 477 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 579 594 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 595 604 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 665 680 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 681 690 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1220 1235 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1416 1425 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1559 1574 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
Breakpoint reuse has been reported at the cytological [54,89-91] and the molecular level [16,25-27,92]. Based on our phylogenetic reconstruction of the chromosomal rearrangements of the species considered here (Table 1), it is clear that some ancestral gene configurations have been disrupted independently more than once during the evolution of the subgenus Sophophora. Using sequences from D. ananassae, D. persimilis, and D. pseudoobscura as outgroups to the D. melanogaster species subgroup, we found evidence for breakage in 17 out of the 55 (~31%) regions disrupted in the D. melanogaster/D. yakuba lineage. We also see evidence for nonrandom breakage in the D. melanogaster/D. yakuba complex, i.e., at a relatively short phylogenetic distance. For each of the three pairs of inversions 3L(3)/3L(4), 3R(7)/3R(8), and 3R(10)/3R(11), three, instead of four, breakpoint regions are involved. This recurrent breakage might denote structural instability of particular genomic regions. For example, CG9579, one of the genes adjacent to the breakpoints of the inversion X(5), is also linked to a remarkable set of molecular reorganizations associated with the birth of a multigene family of a chimeric gene, Sdic, on the D. melanogaster lineage [93]. Additional support for structural instability of inversion breakpoint regions comes from the fact that one breakpoint region of inversion 2LR(4), which occurs on the D. yakuba lineage, uses the same genomic interval that has independently permitted the recent evolution of an unusually high TE density in the D. melanogaster lineage (HDR13 in [94]).
###end p 42
###begin p 43
###xml 154 156 154 156 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b037">37</xref>
###xml 311 313 311 313 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b051">51</xref>
###xml 314 316 314 316 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b092">92</xref>
###xml 393 402 393 402 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 407 416 407 416 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. erecta</named-content>
###xml 418 425 418 425 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 568 577 568 577 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. erecta</named-content>
###xml 582 591 582 591 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 772 781 772 781 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 786 796 786 796 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. erecta,</italic>
###xml 896 905 896 905 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 910 919 910 919 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. erecta</named-content>
###xml 393 402 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 407 416 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
###xml 568 577 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
###xml 582 591 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 772 781 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 786 795 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
###xml 896 905 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 910 919 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
A related issue to breakpoint reuse is the possibility that the same inversion can arise twice. The unique origin of inversions has been challenged (see [37] for discussion), but in the two cases considered to be the most convincing, experimental evidence has not supported a polyphyletic origin of inversions [51,92]. Fourteen breakpoint regions are associated with shared inversions between D. yakuba and D. erecta (Table 1), which indicates that the same gene pairs have been disrupted and reorganized in the same way, suggesting a common origin in the ancestor of D. erecta and D. yakuba. Comparative sequence analysis at the nucleotide level for those 14 junctions failed to find evidence of an independent origin of these inversions in the lineages that lead to the D. yakuba and D. erecta, although it must be noted that our power of detection can be compromised by the time elapsed since D. yakuba and D. erecta shared an ancestor.
###end p 43
###begin title 44
Inversion Breakpoints Can Disrupt Large- and Small-Scale Gene Domains
###end title 44
###begin p 45
###xml 139 141 139 141 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b028">28</xref>
###xml 606 608 606 608 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b095">95</xref>
###xml 621 623 621 623 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b029">29</xref>
Expression profiling of the genomes of several species has shown that co-expressed genes tend to co-locate in the genome (for review, see [28]). The biological significance of co-expression clustering is still poorly understood, but if these "transcriptional territories" represent functional associations among neighboring genes, natural selection should prevent their disruption. Conservation of clusters across lineages differentiated by the accumulation of multiple chromosomal rearrangements has been interpreted as support for the functional association of clusters of co-expressed genes in mammals [95] and flies [29].
###end p 45
###begin p 46
###xml 3 19 3 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster,</italic>
###xml 182 184 182 184 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b096">96</xref>
###xml 185 187 185 187 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b099">99</xref>
###xml 252 254 252 254 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b097">97</xref>
###xml 296 311 296 311 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 501 516 501 516 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster</italic>
###xml 521 531 521 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 581 583 581 583 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b097">97</xref>
###xml 601 604 601 604 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Try</italic>
###xml 651 660 651 660 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 928 947 928 947 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG12388 (kappaTry),</italic>
###xml 988 1006 988 1006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG12387 (zetaTry),</italic>
###xml 3 18 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 296 311 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 501 516 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 521 530 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 651 660 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
In D. melanogaster, the preferential clustering of genes, by the time or place of their expression, has been reported based on both expressed sequence tag (EST) and microarray data [96-99]. In a study of the distribution of sex-biased gene expression [97], 75% of the genes on Release 3.1 of the D. melanogaster genome were assayed. Fifteen gene clusters that are expressed either in testis, in ovary, or in the soma were found. Despite the relatively small number of gene-order interruptions between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba, one of the clusters identified by Parisi et al. [97], containing the Try multigene family, is broken in the lineage of D. yakuba by inversion 2LR(8). At least eight out of ten members of the disrupted gene cluster are highly expressed in the soma. The disruption of this transcriptional territory may be related to the fact that the chromosomal breakage occurred between a member of the cluster, CG12388 (kappaTry), which is soma-biased in expression, and CG12387 (zetaTry), which is not.
###end p 46
###begin p 47
###xml 97 112 97 112 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 114 117 114 117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b100">100</xref>
###xml 146 161 146 161 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 602 617 602 617 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 626 628 626 628 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b098">98</xref>
###xml 867 870 867 870 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b100">100</xref>
###xml 937 962 937 962 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster/D. yakuba</italic>
###xml 1121 1122 1121 1122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G</italic>
###xml 1122 1125 1122 1125 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">adj</sub>
###xml 1133 1137 1133 1137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d.f.</italic>
###xml 1143 1144 1143 1144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1234 1243 1234 1243 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1434 1449 1434 1449 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1594 1604 1594 1604 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba.</italic>
###xml 1820 1835 1820 1835 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1840 1850 1840 1850 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba.</italic>
###xml 97 112 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 146 161 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 602 617 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 937 952 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 953 962 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1234 1243 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1434 1449 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1594 1603 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1820 1835 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1840 1849 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Transcriptional territories have been found to be correlated with the DNA replication program in D. melanogaster [100]. Specifically, 7.5% of the D. melanogaster genome, distributed in 52 well-defined regions, is under-replicated in polytene chromosomes, and 50 of these regions also replicate late during the S period in cultured Kc cells; other regions present a non-delayed replication status in at least one of the two tissues. Sixty percent (30/50) of these late or under-replicating regions are associated with previously defined transcriptional territories; these domains account for 20% of the D. melanogaster genome [98]. Globally, transcriptional territories with a delayed pattern of DNA replication seem to be enriched for genes expressed in the testis and during pupal development, and depleted of genes expressed in the ovary and embryonic development [100]. Are the 55 gene pairs disrupted by inversion breakpoints in the D. melanogaster/D. yakuba lineages randomly distributed across the genome with regard to their replication status? We did not find a significant deviation from the random expectation (Gadj= 5.29; d.f. = 3; p = 0.15); however, we did find that three out of the 53 ancestral gene pairs disrupted in D. yakuba (Xm(8), 2m(19), and 3m(45)) are embedded in regions that are under-replicated in salivary glands and late replicated in Kc cells. These results show that at least some of the regions of the D. melanogaster genome, within which genes have a similar expression profile and/or replication program, are not necessarily conserved between this species and D. yakuba. This suggests that either those domains have little adaptive value, supporting the idea of accidental co-expression, or that their adaptive value has evolved recently, relative to the time of the divergence between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba.
###end p 47
###begin p 48
###xml 29 44 29 44 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 95 98 95 98 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b101">101</xref>
###xml 211 214 211 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b102">102</xref>
###xml 215 218 215 218 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b103">103</xref>
###xml 263 273 263 273 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 347 354 347 354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 389 398 389 398 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 525 533 525 533 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st005">Table S5</xref>
###xml 576 584 576 584 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050152-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 702 716 702 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">(CG9578-CG9579</italic>
###xml 721 737 721 737 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG31142-CG5289),</italic>
###xml 792 801 792 801 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 879 894 879 894 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 926 935 926 935 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 29 44 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 263 272 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 389 398 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 792 801 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 879 894 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 926 935 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Some 1,027 pairs of genes in D. melanogaster have overlapping transcripts in opposite strands [101]. Antisense overlap can play an important role in regulating gene expression at the post-transcriptional level [102,103]. Five of these genes pairs are disjunct in D. yakuba, as a consequence of an inversion breakpoint. Comparison across lineages (Table 1) indicates that the disruption in D. yakuba represents the derived state. The five inversions that disrupt antisense pairs are all associated with inverted duplications (Table S5). Our model for the origin of inversions (Figure 2) can account for the conservation of sequences of decoupled antisense pairs of genes. At least in two of these cases (CG9578-CG9579 and CG31142-CG5289), the 3' UTR sequences of the independent gene pairs of D. yakuba are very similar in sequence and in length to their corresponding 3' UTRs in D. melanogaster. In the other three cases, the D. yakuba 3' UTR of one of the members of each pair is truncated.
###end p 48
###begin title 49
Conclusion
###end title 49
###begin p 50
###xml 86 96 86 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 195 210 195 210 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 215 224 215 224 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 348 357 348 357 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 421 436 421 436 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 839 842 839 842 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b104">104</xref>
###xml 843 846 843 846 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b105">105</xref>
###xml 951 954 951 954 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b106">106</xref>
###xml 1128 1130 1128 1130 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b046">46</xref>
###xml 1131 1133 1131 1133 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b075">75</xref>
###xml 1134 1136 1134 1136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b076">76</xref>
###xml 1272 1287 1272 1287 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 195 210 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 215 224 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 348 357 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 421 436 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1272 1287 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
This work unveils novel aspects of the evolution of the molecular organization of the Drosophila genome in particular and of the genomes of insects in general. The use of genome sequence data of D. melanogaster and D. yakuba has proven to be useful in reconstructing the history of genome rearrangements in these species. The lineage that leads to D. yakuba is evolving substantially faster at the chromosomal level than D. melanogaster (28:1); nevertheless, the mechanism that underlies the generation of many inversions (~59%) in both lineages is the same, and it seems to be initiated by the presence of staggered breaks, which in turn enables the generation of duplications in inverted orientation of sequences at co-occurrent breakpoint regions. These duplications diverge mainly by both nucleotide substitutions and small deletions [104,105], and can contribute, as do segmental duplications in mammals, to the diversification of gene function [106]. A model of inversion generation based on staggered breaks, either isochromatid or chromatid, contrasts with a model of ectopic recombination between repetitive sequences [46,75,76]. Our data also give clear evidence, at the molecular level, of the reuse of the same breakpoint region and that expression domains in D. melanogaster may be disrupted in other species, bringing into question their potential adaptive significance.
###end p 50
###begin p 51
###xml 47 57 47 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
The availability of complete sequences from 12 Drosophila species now offers the opportunity to extend the analysis of chromosome evolution at a molecular level. Several fundamental questions remain: whether or not mechanisms of inversion formation are general across taxa; and whether there are functional constraints on chromosomal evolution, and, if so, at what level do these operate.
###end p 51
###begin title 52
Materials and Methods
###end title 52
###begin title 53
Flies.
###end title 53
###begin p 54
###xml 45 60 45 60 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 172 183 172 183 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. simulans</named-content>
###xml 230 239 230 239 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 45 60 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 172 183 <span type="species:ncbi:7240">D. simulans</span>
###xml 230 239 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
The following species and strains were used: D. melanogaster (OR-R from the Department of Genetics, University of Cambridge, and Zimbabwe 2 from D. L. Hartl's laboratory); D. simulans (Sim-1 from Chapel Hill, North Carolina); and D. yakuba (Tai18E2 from the Tucson Stock Center). In the case of Zimbabwe 2 and Tai18E2, we checked whether they were homokaryotypic by visually examining salivary gland polytene chromosome preparations stained with orcein. In the case of Zimbabwe 2, we detected two paracentric inversions in a sample of 20 autosomal genomes and 16 X chromosome genomes. No gross chromosomal polymorphisms were detected in a sample of 20 autosomal genomes and 16 X chromosome genomes of Tai18E2.
###end p 54
###begin title 55
In situ hybridization of molecular probes onto polytene chromosomes.
###end title 55
###begin p 56
###xml 274 282 274 282 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st007">Table S7</xref>
###xml 365 393 365 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster: y; cn bw sp</italic>
###xml 395 398 395 398 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b107">107</xref>
###xml 472 521 472 521 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG2708 (Tom34), CG7918, CG31176, CG34034, CG5289,</italic>
###xml 526 540 526 540 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG6576 (Glec);</italic>
###xml 574 603 574 603 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HDC14860, HDC14861, HDC14862,</italic>
###xml 608 616 608 616 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HDC12400</italic>
###xml 618 620 618 620 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b060">60</xref>
###xml 643 650 643 650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdf800,</italic>
###xml 712 716 712 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">-fos</italic>
###xml 965 968 965 968 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b108">108</xref>
###xml 1168 1183 1168 1183 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1185 1188 1185 1188 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b109">109</xref>
###xml 1279 1287 1279 1287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HDC14860</italic>
###xml 1292 1301 1292 1301 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HDC14861,</italic>
###xml 1364 1373 1364 1373 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 161 169 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">Children</span>
###xml 365 380 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1168 1183 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1364 1373 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Five BACs and 11 genomic clones were used as molecular probes. The BAC clones (BACR07M14, BACR45A07, BACR16N15, BACR42I20, and BACR08K01) were obtained from the Children's Hospital Oakland Research Institute. Genomic clones were PCR amplified using the primers described in Table S7. The genomic DNA used for the PCR amplifications was from the sequenced strain of D. melanogaster: y; cn bw sp [107]. The genomic fragments generated correspond to the protein-coding genes CG2708 (Tom34), CG7918, CG31176, CG34034, CG5289, and CG6576 (Glec); the putatively transcribed genes HDC14860, HDC14861, HDC14862, and HDC12400 [60]; and the sequence of pdf800, which is said to be related to the mammalian proto-oncogene c-fos. Cloning of PCR products and preparation of DNA from recombinant clones was performed using conventional methods. In the case of BAC clones, we used the methods described at . In situ hybridization of probes to polytene chromosomes was done as in [108]. Detection of the hybridization signals was done by phase contrast with a Zeiss Axioskop 2 (Carl Zeiss, ). Chromosomal localization was determined using the photographic polytene chromosome maps of D. melanogaster [109]. All the probes yielded one or two hybridization signals with the exception of those for HDC14860 and HDC14861, which failed to generate a detectable hybridization signal in D. yakuba under the experimental conditions used.
###end p 56
###begin title 57
###xml 12 21 12 21 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 12 21 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Assembly of D. yakuba supercontigs into chromosomal sequences.
###end title 57
###begin p 58
###xml 35 44 35 44 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 427 436 427 436 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 471 480 471 480 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 521 536 521 536 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 615 630 615 630 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 674 683 674 683 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 749 764 749 764 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 826 836 826 836 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 972 988 972 988 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster.</italic>
###xml 1075 1084 1075 1084 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1159 1174 1159 1174 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 35 44 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 427 436 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 471 480 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 521 536 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 615 630 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 674 683 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 749 764 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 826 835 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 972 987 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1075 1084 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1159 1174 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
The sequencing and assembly of the D. yakuba genome will be described elsewhere (D. J. Begun, A. K. Holloway, K. Stevens, L. W. Hillier, Y.-P. Poh, M. W. Hahn, P. M. Nista, C. D. Jones, A. D. Kern, C. Dewey, L. Pachter, E. Myers, and C. H. Langley, unpublished data). To create chromosomal assignments and ordering of "supercontigs" (gapped scaffolds of ungapped contigs as defined by mate pairs) along the chromosomes for the D. yakuba genome assembly, contigs from the D. yakuba assembly that uniquely aligned with the D. melanogaster genome were identified and then ordered by their positions along the assigned D. melanogaster chromosomes. This process resulted in some D. yakuba supercontigs with contigs that aligned to different regions of a D. melanogaster chromosome. To assemble supercontigs into chromosome arms in D. yakuba, reversals of the tiling path of mapped contigs were introduced to "rejoin" those supercontigs that had been split by the alignments to D. melanogaster. The overall goal was to minimize the total number of reversals required to rejoin all D. yakuba supercontigs previously assigned to disjoint chromosomal regions based on D. melanogaster alignments. We note that reversals were introduced only between contigs (not within contigs) and the process was not gene based.
###end p 58
###begin title 59
###xml 29 39 29 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba.</italic>
###xml 29 38 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Gene-order reconstruction in D. yakuba.
###end title 59
###begin p 60
###xml 39 54 39 54 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 171 186 171 186 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 246 255 246 255 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 441 444 441 444 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;30</sup>
###xml 485 493 485 493 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st008">Table S8</xref>
###xml 558 567 558 567 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 736 739 736 739 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;30</sup>
###xml 974 983 974 983 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1003 1012 1003 1012 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1039 1055 1039 1055 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster,</italic>
###xml 1336 1345 1336 1345 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-sg007">Figure S7</xref>
###xml 1357 1359 1357 1359 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b072">72</xref>
###xml 1453 1468 1453 1468 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1482 1492 1482 1492 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 1508 1511 1508 1511 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b110">110</xref>
###xml 1583 1592 1583 1592 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 1869 1884 1869 1884 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1889 1899 1889 1899 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 39 54 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 171 186 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 246 255 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 558 567 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 974 983 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1003 1012 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1039 1054 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1453 1468 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1482 1491 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1583 1592 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1869 1884 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1889 1898 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
The complete set of transcripts of the D. melanogaster Release 4.1 annotation was downloaded from UCSC Genome Browser (). This set represents 13,449 annotated genes. Each D. melanogaster transcript was used as a query against the assembly of the D. yakuba genome release 2.0 (WUSTL November 2005, the droYak2 assembly) using BLASTN 2.2.2 with default settings and then filtered for the top hit for each transcript with a cutoff E-value of 10-30; the nonfiltered output can be found as Table S8. This approach localized 12,690 genes on the genome sequence of D. yakuba with a best hit on the same chromosome arm (with exceptions made for genes inside the pericentric inversion on chromosome 2); 320 genes had no BLASTN hit higher than 10-30, and 429 genes hit unmapped scaffolds or gave multiple hits with equal E-value in more than one chromosome arm. Genes unambiguously localized were sorted into chromosome order (centromere to telomere) for the six Muller's elements of D. yakuba. The gene order in D. yakuba was compared with that of D. melanogaster, and gene-order interruptions between the two species were inferred; the two genes flanking each gene-order interruption were taken as the limits of different syntenic blocks. This method will not reliably detect very small rearrangements, although we know that these occur (e.g., Figure S7; see also [72]). For calculating the minimum number of inversions necessary to transform the gene order of D. melanogaster into that of D. yakuba, we used GRIMM [110]. Estimates on the size of syntenic blocks and regions between them in D. yakuba were obtained by taking into account the coordinates of the BLASTN hits of the outermost markers of each syntenic block. In the case of transposition events, we examined the nonfiltered output for genes whose BLAST hits were surrounded by different pairs of flanking genes in D. melanogaster and D. yakuba, especially those with unambiguous hits in different Muller's elements.
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 147 156 147 156 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 635 645 635 645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 949 958 949 958 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 147 156 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 635 644 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 949 958 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
One complicating factor in our analysis is that BLASTN of a region including 3R:3862326-3867817 was highly similar to two different regions of the D. yakuba assembly: one on Contig690 (currently assembled into chromosome arm 3R), and one, with a slightly lower match, on Contig706 (currently assigned to the "random" bin of chromosome arm 3R because it seemed to overlap Contig690). Contig690 has a sequence coverage of 5.8-8.3x, Contig706 of 3-4.7x. The overall coverage of the genome is 9.4x, but the supercontigs of chromosome arms 2R and 3R have approximately 12x coverage. Were this region to be truly duplicated in the genome of D. yakuba, we would expect the sum of the coverage of Contigs 690 and 706 to be at the very least 18x, rather than (at most) 13x. In situ hybridization to polytene chromosomes of probes from this region shows only a single site, that expected on chromosome arm 3R. Residual heterozygosity for other regions of the D. yakuba sequence has been experimentally verified (J. Comeron and C. Langley, personal communication), and we interpret these two hits as being the consequence of heterozygosity in the genome.
###end p 61
###begin title 62
###xml 81 90 81 90 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 81 90 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Experimental verification of the molecular organization at breakpoint regions in D. yakuba.
###end title 62
###begin p 63
###xml 58 73 58 73 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 78 88 78 88 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 210 220 210 220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 299 307 299 307 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st001">Table S1</xref>
###xml 917 932 917 932 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 968 976 968 976 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050152-st007">Table S7</xref>
###xml 58 73 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 78 87 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 210 219 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 917 932 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
To confirm the predicted gene-order interruptions between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba, we cloned and sequence verified the transition between adjacent syntenic blocks of 27 (49%) of the breakpoint regions in D. yakuba, namely Xy(9), Xy(10), 2y(19-24), 2y(26-28), 3y(35-43), 3y(46-51), and 3y(53) (Table S1). We extracted genomic DNA from the sequenced strain Tai18E2 by conventional methods. We designed primers to amplify the sequence that spans the transition between syntenic blocks. In a few cases, either because of the size of the region between the neighboring reference genes or because of technical difficulties, we amplified sets of overlapping segments that ensured coverage of the transition between adjacent syntenic blocks. PCR products were cloned into a pCR2.1 Topo Vector (Invitrogen, ). Sequencing reactions of the two ends of each clone were done, and the reads were aligned by BLAST against the D. melanogaster genome. Primers used are listed in Table S7.
###end p 63
###begin title 64
###xml 43 52 43 52 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 57 73 57 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster.</italic>
###xml 43 52 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 57 72 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
Sequence analysis of breakpoint regions in D. yakuba and D. melanogaster.
###end title 64
###begin p 65
###xml 29 44 29 44 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 64 73 64 73 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 245 255 245 255 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba,</italic>
###xml 268 284 268 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster,</italic>
###xml 325 340 325 340 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 520 523 520 523 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b111">111</xref>
###xml 538 541 538 541 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b112">112</xref>
###xml 703 718 703 718 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 886 888 886 888 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;8</sup>
###xml 1226 1241 1226 1241 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1929 1939 1929 1939 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 1959 1975 1959 1975 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster.</italic>
###xml 2065 2080 2065 2080 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 2206 2215 2206 2215 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 2373 2402 2373 2402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster, D. simulans,</italic>
###xml 2407 2416 2407 2416 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. erecta</named-content>
###xml 29 44 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 64 73 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 245 254 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 268 283 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 325 340 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 703 718 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1226 1241 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1959 1974 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 2065 2080 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 2206 2215 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 2373 2388 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 2390 2401 <span type="species:ncbi:7240">D. simulans</span>
###xml 2407 2416 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
Because not all the genes of D. melanogaster were mapped to the D. yakuba assembly, and because there may have been transpositions of regions during the evolution of these genomes, we extracted the sequences of the 55 genomic discontinuities of D. yakuba, relative to D. melanogaster, and aligned these by BLASTN against the D. melanogaster genome. This refined the limits of the syntenic blocks and allowed their ends to be precisely mapped. To identify duplicates at co-occurrent breakpoint regions, we used PipMaker [111], and BLAST2 [112] with their default parameters. Sequences from all local alignments spanning more than 40 bp from PipMaker were used as queries in a BLASTN analysis against the D. melanogaster genome, thereby verifying their identities and genomic locations. We did the same with the BLAST2 output for those sequences with hits whose E-value were lower than 10-8 and were at least 40-bp long. Both approaches provided essentially the same results. Nucleotide identities between particular duplicates and their reference sequences were derived from the BLAST2 analysis. For genes that are adjacent to breakpoints and/or are affected by them, we did an additional BLAST2 analysis, using as queries the D. melanogaster sequences of their transcripts. Sequences that are now found as inverted duplications at co-occurrent breakpoint regions may not necessarily have been in this orientation immediately after the occurrence of the inversion, because subsequent events may have taken place. For this reason, we reconstructed the most parsimonious history of each inversion in an attempt to establish the sequence immediately after each had occurred. We analyzed the presence of TE sequences using the RepeatMasker track from UCSC (RepBase libraries: RepBase Update 9.11 and RM database version 20050112) and subsequently by BLAST2 analysis using a collection of TE sequences that includes those in different Drosophila species other than D. melanogaster. All the significant hits found by our BLAST2 analysis correspond to footprints of TEs of D. melanogaster previously detected with RepeatMasker. For duplications that spanned noncoding regions, we did a BLASTN analysis against the D. yakuba genome, in order to determine that they did not include repetitive sequences. When necessary, we proceeded in an identical manner with breakpoint regions of D. melanogaster, D. simulans, and D. erecta.
###end p 65
###begin title 66
###xml 72 87 72 87 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 92 102 92 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba.</italic>
###xml 72 87 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 92 101 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Phylogenetic status of the gene configurations at breakpoint regions of D. melanogaster and D. yakuba.
###end title 66
###begin p 67
###xml 82 97 82 97 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 104 113 104 113 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 196 211 196 211 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 416 431 416 431 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 436 445 436 445 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 470 485 470 485 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 510 521 510 521 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. simulans</named-content>
###xml 553 562 553 562 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 584 593 584 593 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. erecta</named-content>
###xml 621 633 621 633 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. ananassae</named-content>
###xml 661 674 661 674 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. persimilis</named-content>
###xml 705 721 705 721 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. pseudoobscura</named-content>
###xml 855 864 855 864 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 869 879 869 879 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. erecta.</italic>
###xml 916 927 916 927 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">independent</italic>
###xml 82 97 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 104 113 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 196 211 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 416 431 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 436 445 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 470 485 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 510 521 <span type="species:ncbi:7240">D. simulans</span>
###xml 553 562 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 584 593 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
###xml 621 633 <span type="species:ncbi:7217">D. ananassae</span>
###xml 661 674 <span type="species:ncbi:374970|species:ncbi:7234">D. persimilis</span>
###xml 705 721 <span type="species:ncbi:7237">D. pseudoobscura</span>
###xml 855 864 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 869 878 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
In order to determine whether the gene configuration in the breakpoint regions in D. melanogaster or in D. yakuba is ancestral or derived, i.e., the result of a chromosomal rearrangement, we took D. melanogaster as a reference, and we determined whether or not the reference genes within a particular breakpoint region were adjacent in a set of species selected on the basis of their phylogenetic relationships with D. melanogaster and D. yakuba. Specifically, we used: D. melanogaster (Release 4.1; FlyBase); D. simulans (release 1.0 Apr. 2005; UCSC); D. yakuba (droYak2 Nov. 2005); D. erecta (droEre1 Aug. 2005; UCSC); D. ananassae (droAna2 Aug. 2005; UCSC); D. persimilis (droPer1 Oct. 2005 UCSC); and D. pseudoobscura (Release 1.0; S. W. Schaeffer, personal communication). We used PipMaker to analyze the breakpoint regions apparently shared between D. yakuba and D. erecta. If these breakpoint regions were of independent origin, then we would expect to see discontinuities and indels between them. In fact, in all cases, the evidence suggests that these "shared" breakpoints were the consequence of a single ancestral event.
###end p 67

###begin title 69
###xml 40 50 40 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>

Phylogenetic Relationships in the Genus Drosophila and Its Subgenera: Drosophila and Sophophora
###end title 69
###begin p 70
###xml 123 133 123 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sophophora</italic>
###xml 139 151 139 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">melanogaster</italic>
###xml 361 363 361 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b054">54</xref>
###xml 364 367 364 367 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b113">113</xref>
###xml 368 371 368 371 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b115">115</xref>
###xml 404 419 404 419 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. melanogaster</italic>
###xml 433 461 433 461 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. mauritiana, D. sechellia,</italic>
###xml 466 478 466 478 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. simulans,</italic>
###xml 494 541 494 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. erecta, D. orena, D. santomea, D. teissieri,</italic>
###xml 546 555 546 555 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 601 603 601 603 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b042">42</xref>
###xml 404 419 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 433 446 <span type="species:ncbi:7226">D. mauritiana</span>
###xml 448 460 <span type="species:ncbi:7238">D. sechellia</span>
###xml 466 477 <span type="species:ncbi:7240">D. simulans</span>
###xml 494 503 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
###xml 505 513 <span type="species:ncbi:7233">D. orena</span>
###xml 515 526 <span type="species:ncbi:129105">D. santomea</span>
###xml 528 540 <span type="species:ncbi:7243">D. teissieri</span>
###xml 546 555 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
The phylogenetic relationships among the species used in the present study are shown in detail. All belong to the subgenus Sophophora. The melanogaster species subgroup comprises nine species, which have been commonly clustered into two complexes by the criteria of gene sequences, polytene chromosome banding pattern, and the structures of the male genitalia [54,113-115]. One of the complexes includes D. melanogaster and the trio D. mauritiana, D. sechellia, and D. simulans, and the second D. erecta, D. orena, D. santomea, D. teissieri, and D. yakuba. All the divergences times are according to [42].

###begin title 81

###begin title 89
###xml 68 83 68 83 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 88 97 88 97 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 68 83 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 88 97 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Large-Scale Comparison of the Muller's Elements A, D, and E between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba
###end title 89
###begin p 90
###xml 178 181 178 181 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b116">116</xref>
###xml 283 298 283 298 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 303 312 303 312 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 334 349 334 349 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 753 762 753 762 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 809 818 809 818 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050152-g002">Figures 2</xref>
###xml 849 857 849 857 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG14187,</italic>
###xml 912 920 912 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG34034,</italic>
###xml 999 1006 999 1006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG9925,</italic>
###xml 1154 1160 1154 1160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG9925</italic>
###xml 1176 1182 1176 1182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG9925</italic>
###xml 1202 1217 1202 1217 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1222 1231 1222 1231 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 283 298 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 303 312 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 334 349 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 753 762 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 1202 1217 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1222 1231 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
(A), Muller's element A (chromosome X); (B) Muller's elements D and E (chromosome 3). The outermost protein-coding genes of consecutive syntenic blocks are indicated. Following [116], syntenic blocks (defined as regions in which the relative gene order is globally conserved between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba) are numbered taking D. melanogaster as a reference and in an increasing order from the telomere of chromosome X (number 1) to the telomere of the right arm of chromosome 3 (number 58); an arrowhead indicates the orientation of the segments. Lines between chromosomes match homologous syntenic blocks between species. Solid triangles correspond to genes that were duplicated during the generation of inversions in the lineage that leads to D. yakuba following a model of staggered strand breaks (Figures 2, S2, and S3). Those genes are CG14187, which was generated by the inversion X(1) in (A), and CG34034, which was generated by the inversion 3R(7) in (B). Open triangle denotes gene CG9925, whose relocation can be explained by a conservative transposition event or, alternatively, by two paracentric inversions that overlap by one gene, CG9925. The fact that CG9925 is flanked both in D. melanogaster and D. yakuba by genes that, in their turn, are the outermost markers of different syntenic blocks strongly supports the second explanation.
###end p 90

###begin title 93
Different Evolutionary Scenarios That Can Lead to the Presence of Inversion-Mediated Duplications at Only One of the Two Co-occurrent Breakpoint Regions
###end title 93
###begin p 94
###xml 42 57 42 57 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 87 96 87 96 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 42 57 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 87 96 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
The inversion X(1) is used as an example. D. melanogaster (top gene configuration) and D. yakuba (bottom gene configuration).
###end p 94
###begin p 95
###xml 93 100 93 100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG14817</italic>
###xml 105 113 105 113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HDC18578</italic>
###xml 198 206 198 206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HDC18578</italic>
(A) Scenario involving four staggered breakpoints (arrows). In this case, the duplication of CG14817 and HDC18578 is coupled with the generation of the inversion. Subsequently, one of the copies of HDC18578 degenerates by accumulating nucleotide substitutions and indels so that it is no longer recognizable.
###end p 95
###begin p 96
###xml 126 133 126 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG14817</italic>
(B) Scenario involving staggered breakpoints at one genomic region and a single-strand break at the other. In this case, only CG14817 becomes duplicated as a result of the inversion.
###end p 96
###begin p 97
###xml 144 162 144 162 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D. yakuba, CG14817</italic>
###xml 178 186 178 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HDC18578</italic>
###xml 144 153 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
The outcome of both scenarios is identical. Coding sequences that have undergone an inversion-mediated duplication in the lineage that leads to D. yakuba, CG14817 (in green) and HDC18578 (in pink) are indicated by a gradient.

###xml 78 93 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 98 107 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
Inversions Required to Transform the Gene Arrangement of Chromosome 2 between D. melanogaster and D. yakuba
###end title 101
###begin p 102
###xml 158 161 158 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050152-b110">110</xref>
###xml 351 358 351 358 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0050152-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 472 481 472 481 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 486 495 486 495 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. erecta</named-content>
###xml 627 636 627 636 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 641 650 641 650 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. erecta</named-content>
###xml 705 713 705 713 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050152-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 729 738 729 738 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. yakuba</named-content>
###xml 791 806 791 806 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 472 481 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 486 495 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
###xml 627 636 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 641 650 <span type="species:ncbi:280662|species:ncbi:203672|species:ncbi:167917|species:ncbi:491826|species:ncbi:7220">D. erecta</span>
###xml 729 738 <span type="species:ncbi:7245">D. yakuba</span>
###xml 791 806 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
The diagram shows 11 inversions, one pericentric and ten paracentric. Other scenarios obtained with GRIMM involve the same number of reversals of gene order [110]. Duplications at breakpoint regions, disruption of multigene families and antisense overlapping, and gene organization in outgroup species are the criteria used to infer the polarization (Table 1). Using this information, the inversions 2L(3), 2R(11), and 2LR(5) occurred first because all are shared between D. yakuba and D. erecta. Note that the order of these inversions is arbitrary. The other inversions took place after the split of the lineage that lead to D. yakuba and D. erecta. The numbering of the syntenic blocks follows that of Figure 3; the blocks of D. yakuba appear with a minus sign if inverted in relation to D. melanogaster.

A few cases of departures from perfect collinearity are observed denoting small rearrangements. We thank the following centers for providing genomic data: Genome Sequencing Center at the Washington University School of Medicine in St. Louis (D. simulans and D. yakuba); Agencourt (D. ananassae and D. erecta); the Broad Institute (D. persimilis); and the Baylor Genome Sequencing Center (D. pseudoobscura). We are very grateful for the initiative of Charles Langley and David Begun in writing the White Paper that led to the funding of the sequencing of D. simulans and D. yakuba. We also thank: Cahir O'Kane for his help in microscopy; Steve Russell for providing the genomic DNA of D. melanogaster; Rosa Bautista-Llacer, Theresa Heffernan, and Edward Ryder for technical assistance; Francoise Balloux, Rhona Borts, Kevin Hiom, Steve Jackson, John Parsch, and Sebastian Ramos-Onsins for advice on different aspects of the analyses; and Stepan Belyakin, Craig Nelson, Michael Parisi, and Stephen Schaeffer for providing unpublished datasets. Finally, we are indebted to Walter Eanes, Evan Eichler, Jeffrey Powell, Stephen Schaeffer, the Academic Editor, and three anonymous reviewers for helpful comments on the manuscript, and especially to Igor Sharakhov for pointing out that staggered double-strand breaks of paired chromatids can generate a pattern of inverted duplications indistinguishable from those that would result from a model of staggered single-strand breaks of an isochromatid. JMR was supported by a European Molecular Biology Organization (EMBO) long-term fellowship, and CMB was supported by a USA Research Fellowship from the Royal Society.
